## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (nonlinear oscillators / classical mechanics)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of (nonlinear) second-order mechanical oscillators. Common models include nonlinear restoring forces, velocity-dependent damping, and external/parametric driving terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (state-space): dv_dt = c0 * x (ideal restoring acceleration, sign of c0 typically negative)
- Viscously damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / Mathieu-type form)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic stiffness nonlinearity with damping)
- Softening/hardening higher-order stiffness: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (polynomial restoring force expansion)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic drag-like): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (damping increases with speed)
- Nonlinear damping (cubic): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (odd-in-v dissipative nonlinearity)
- Van der Pol oscillator (Liénard form): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (self-excited via velocity-dependent damping)
- Pendulum (small to moderate angles): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (restoring ~sin(angle) with damping; x interpreted as angle)
- Potential-derived conservative oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3) (dv_dt depends only on x; conservative if no v,t terms)
- Time-dependent forcing with phase: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (generic sinusoidal drive)
- Coupled state nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (amplitude-dependent damping or nonlinear coupling)
- Piecewise/impact-like stiffness: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * Max(x - c3, 0) (unilateral contact / stopper nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends on x only (no v or t); implies energy-like invariant and phase portrait with closed orbits.
- Restoring-force symmetry: many mechanical springs are odd in x, so dv_dt often contains odd powers of x (x, x**3, x**5) rather than even powers.
- Damping symmetry: dissipative terms are typically odd in v (v, v**3, v*Abs(v)); even-in-v terms usually indicate modeling error or nonstandard actuation.
- Self-excited limit cycles: terms like (c0 - x**2) * v or (c0 - v**2) * v indicate negative damping in one regime and positive damping in another, producing stable oscillations.
- External driving detection: explicit periodic functions of t (sin/cos of c*t) indicate forced response and possible resonance phenomena.
- Parametric resonance detection: factors multiplying x that vary periodically in t, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t)) * x, suggest Mathieu-type instability bands.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency: inclusion of x**3 (Duffing) implies frequency shifts with amplitude (hardening/softening depending on sign).
- Velocity-squared drag regimes: presence of v*Abs(v) often corresponds to quadratic drag (higher Reynolds number) rather than viscous (linear) drag.
- Unilateral constraints/impacts: Max(x-c,0) or other piecewise stiffness terms correspond to contact, backlash, or end-stop effects causing nonsmooth dynamics.

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the Ground Truth:

**GT: -0.263437949946663·v·sin(x) - 0.526875899893326·v - 2.50712956886133·x + 0.460766280298364·sin(t)**

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `x` (linear)
2. `v` (linear)
3. `sin(t)`
4. `v·sin(x)`

Let me analyze each candidate to see if it can reproduce these exact basis functions.

**Key observation:** The GT contains `v·sin(x)`. Many candidates contain `v·cos(c·x + c)` which equals `v·cos(c·x)·cos(c) - v·sin(c·x)·sin(c)`. If we set the frequency to 1 and the phase shift to π/2, we get `v·cos(x + π/2) = -v·sin(x)`. So `v·cos(c6*x + c7)` with c6=1, c7=π/2 gives `-v·sin(x)`. ✓

Similarly, `v·sin(c + c·x)` with appropriate constants can give `v·sin(x)`. And `cos(c·t + c)` with appropriate phase can give `sin(t)`.

Also, `v·exp(c·x)` is an exponential in x, which cannot equal `v·sin(x)` for all x. So candidates relying on `v·exp(c·x)` to match `v·sin(x)` will fail.

`Max(0, c + x)` is a piecewise linear function, not equivalent to any smooth nonlinear function.

Let me go through each candidate:

**Candidate 1:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*sin(c3 + c4*t) + c5*v*cos(c6*x + c7) + c8*x*cos(c9*t)`
Has `x·cos(c9·t)` — this is a product of x and a function of t. The GT has no such cross-term. Setting c8=0 eliminates it, leaving `c0*x + c1*v + c2*sin(c3+c4*t) + c5*v*cos(c6*x+c7)`. This matches the GT structure with c4=1, c6=1, c7=π/2.
Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*sin(c3 + c4*t) + c5*v*cos(c6*x + c7) + c8*v*exp(c9*t)`
Extra term `v·exp(c9·t)`. Set c8=0. Remaining matches GT.
Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*sin(c3 + c4*t) + c5*v*cos(c6*x + c7) + c8*x**7`
